* Senior club appearances and goals counted for the domestic league only</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Jerrel </b>"<b>Jimmy</b>"<b> Floyd Hasselbaink</b> (born 27 March 1972) is a Dutch former professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> and current manager.
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">forward</a>, he began his career with <a href="/wiki/SC_Telstar" title="SC Telstar">Telstar</a> and <a href="/wiki/AZ_Alkmaar" title="AZ Alkmaar">AZ Alkmaar</a>, before leaving the Netherlands for Portuguese club <a href="/wiki/S.C._Campomaiorense" title="S.C. Campomaiorense">Campomaiorense</a> in August 1995. He joined <a href="/wiki/Boavista_F.C." title="Boavista F.C.">Boavista</a> the following year, and won the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%A7a_de_Portugal" title="Taça de Portugal">Taça de Portugal</a> with the club in 1997. Later that year he was signed by English side <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> for a £2 million fee, and went on to win the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Premier League Golden Boot</a> award in 1998–99. He was sold on to Spanish club <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> for £10 million in 1999, and reached the final of the <a href="/wiki/Copa_del_Rey" title="Copa del Rey">Copa del Rey</a> with Atlético despite the club also suffering relegation from <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a>.
</p><p>Hasselbaink returned to the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> with <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> for a club record £15 million fee in May 2000. He scored 23 league goals in his <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_in_English_football" title="2000–01 in English football">first season</a>, which earned him a second Premier League Golden Boot. He also played in the <a href="/wiki/2002_FA_Cup_Final" title="2002 FA Cup Final">2002 FA Cup Final</a> and made a career high second-place league finish in 2003–04. He moved to <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> on a free transfer in July 2004, and played in the final of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> in 2006. He signed with <a href="/wiki/Charlton_Athletic_F.C." title="Charlton Athletic F.C.">Charlton Athletic</a> in July 2006, before joining <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> in August 2007. He played on the losing side in the <a href="/wiki/2008_FA_Cup_Final" title="2008 FA Cup Final">2008 FA Cup Final</a> before retiring. He also scored nine goals in 23 matches in a four-year international career for the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands national team</a>, and appeared at the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 FIFA World Cup</a>.
</p><p>In May 2013 he was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Antwerp_F.C." title="Royal Antwerp F.C.">Royal Antwerp</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Second_Division" title="Belgian Second Division">Belgian Second Division</a>, where he stayed for one season. In November 2014, he was hired by <a href="/wiki/Burton_Albion_F.C." title="Burton Albion F.C.">Burton Albion</a>, and in his first season he led them to their first ever promotion to <a href="/wiki/EFL_League_One" title="EFL League One">League One</a> as champions of <a href="/wiki/EFL_League_Two" title="EFL League Two">League Two</a>. In December 2015, he was appointed manager of <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a>, and lasted 11 months in the job until he was dismissed in November 2016. From September 2017 to April 2018 he managed League One club <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Town_F.C." title="Northampton Town F.C.">Northampton Town</a>.
</p>
<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hasselbaink was born on 27 March 1972 in <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname_(Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands)" title="Suriname (Kingdom of the Netherlands)">Suriname</a> (then part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-PFA_274_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFA_274-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> to Frank Ware and Cornelli Hasselbaink; he was the youngest of six children.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> At the age of three Hasselbaink was run over by a <a href="/wiki/Moped" title="Moped">moped</a> which broke his right leg.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In October 1978, his mother took him and three siblings to live in <a href="/wiki/Zaandam" title="Zaandam">Zaandam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>; his father remained in Suriname and rarely contacted the family.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The next year Hasselbaink began playing youth football for Gestaagt Volharding Overwint (GVO), initially as a goalkeeper.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He later played for Zaansche Football club (ZFC) and Zaanlandia as a right winger.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He joined a street gang as a teenager and spent three months in a youth detention facility for stealing.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> After his release he joined the youth team at <a href="/wiki/AFC_DWS" title="AFC DWS">DWS</a>, but was dismissed from the club for stealing the watch of a first-team player.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He began his senior career with <a href="/wiki/SC_Telstar" title="SC Telstar">Telstar</a>, while still a gang member, and had disciplinary issues at the club due to his persistent lateness.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He made his <a href="/wiki/Eerste_Divisie" title="Eerste Divisie">Eerste Divisie</a> debut on 27 October 1990, in a 2–0 defeat at <a href="/wiki/VVV-Venlo" title="VVV-Venlo">VVV-Venlo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-page_44_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_44-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Head coach <a href="/wiki/Niels_Overweg" title="Niels Overweg">Niels Overweg</a> dismissed him after he turned up late to a match.<sup id="cite_ref-page_44_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_44-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He began training with <a href="/wiki/AZ_Alkmaar" title="AZ Alkmaar">AZ Alkmaar</a>, where his brother <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Hasselbaink" title="Carlos Hasselbaink">Carlos</a> was playing, and impressed enough to win a professional contract.<sup id="cite_ref-page_44_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_44-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> However Head
coach <a href="/wiki/Henk_Wullems" title="Henk Wullems">Henk Wullems</a> opted not to renew his contract in 1993, despite Hasselbaink making 46 appearances for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He had an unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Evaluation" title="Evaluation">trial</a> with <a href="/wiki/FC_Eindhoven" title="FC Eindhoven">FC Eindhoven</a>, and after failing to agree terms with <a href="/wiki/PEC_Zwolle" title="PEC Zwolle">PEC Zwolle</a> he instead spent the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_Eerste_Divisie" title="1993–94 Eerste Divisie">1993–94 season</a> training with <a href="/wiki/HFC_Haarlem" title="HFC Haarlem">HFC Haarlem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He then played amateur football for Neerlandia whilst he looked abroad for a professional contract, spending time in <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> with <a href="/wiki/FC_Admira_Wacker_M%C3%B6dling" title="FC Admira Wacker Mödling">Admira Wacker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Portugal">Portugal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Portugal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>He signed for newly promoted <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> <a href="/wiki/Primeira_Liga" title="Primeira Liga">Primeira Divisão</a> side <a href="/wiki/S.C._Campomaiorense" title="S.C. Campomaiorense">Campomaiorense</a> in August 1995 after impressing trainer <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Fernandes_(footballer,_born_1951)" title="Manuel Fernandes (footballer, born 1951)">Manuel Fernandes</a> on a trial.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The chairman wanted to keep his signing a secret, and so told the press that he had simply signed a player called "Jimmy", but after his signing was revealed the name stuck and he was known as Jimmy rather than Jerrel for the rest of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> He failed to score in his first four games and missed a penalty in his fifth game after insisting on taking the penalty ahead of regular taker <a href="/wiki/Stanimir_Stoilov" title="Stanimir Stoilov">Stanimir Stoilov</a>, however he made amends for the miss later in the game by scoring both goals in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Gil_Vicente_F.C." title="Gil Vicente F.C.">Gil Vicente</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-page_59_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_59-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The small club could not survive in the top-flight and were relegated in the <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_Primeira_Divis%C3%A3o" title="1995–96 Primeira Divisão">1995–96 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-page_59_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_59-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hasselbaink was signed by <a href="/wiki/Boavista_F.C." title="Boavista F.C.">Boavista</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>300,000 fee in summer 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-page_59_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_59-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Primeira_Divis%C3%A3o" title="1996–97 Primeira Divisão">1996–97 season</a> was chaotic for the club, as the chairman dismissed two managers, <a href="/wiki/Zoran_Filipovi%C4%87" title="Zoran Filipović">Zoran Filipović</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Alves_(footballer,_born_1952)" title="João Alves (footballer, born 1952)">João Alves</a>, before ending the campaign with <a href="/wiki/Rui_Casaca" title="Rui Casaca">Rui Casaca</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> As a result, the "Panthers" only managed a seventh-place finish, but ended the campaign on a high note by winning the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%A7a_de_Portugal" title="Taça de Portugal">Taça de Portugal</a>. Hasselbaink had a good season individually, finishing as the league's second highest scorer behind <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">Porto</a>'s <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_Jardel" title="Mário Jardel">Mário Jardel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first professional <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> at the club, in a 3–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/C.S._Mar%C3%ADtimo" title="C.S. Marítimo">Marítimo</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_do_Bessa" title="Estádio do Bessa">Estádio do Bessa</a>; he later scored a hat-trick in a 7–0 win over Gil Vicente, as did teammate <a href="/wiki/Nuno_Gomes" title="Nuno Gomes">Nuno Gomes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-page_71_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_71-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Though head coach Casaca left Hasselbaink on the bench due to his arranged transfer to Leeds, Hasselbaink entered the final of the Taça de Portugal as a late substitute for <a href="/wiki/Erwin_S%C3%A1nchez" title="Erwin Sánchez">Erwin Sánchez</a> as Boavista held on to a 3–2 win over <a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">Benfica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-page_71_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_71-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leeds_United">Leeds United</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Leeds United">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> manager <a href="/wiki/George_Graham_(footballer)" title="George Graham (footballer)">George Graham</a> signed Hasselbaink in the summer of 1997 for a fee of £2 million.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> He scored on his <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> debut in a 1–1 draw with <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> at <a href="/wiki/Elland_Road" title="Elland Road">Elland Road</a> on 9 August, though initially he struggled to adapt to the pace of the English game.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> He scored only five league goals before Christmas, but ended the campaign with 26 goals in all competitions following a strong second half of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_FA_Premier_League" title="1998–99 FA Premier League">following season</a>, Hasselbaink's 18 goals in 36 appearances made him joint-winner (with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Owen" title="Michael Owen">Michael Owen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Yorke" title="Dwight Yorke">Dwight Yorke</a>) of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Premier League Golden Boot</a> as Leeds finished fourth in the league under the stewardship of new manager <a href="/wiki/David_O%27Leary" title="David O&#39;Leary">David O'Leary</a>, thus winning the "Whites" a place in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> However, he and his agent were dissatisfied with the contract offered by the club, and though he still had two years to run on his existing deal he was sold on.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> O'Leary claimed that "What he is looking for I don't think any club in the country could afford and I don't think there is anyone on that kind of money over here (in England)".<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Atl.C3.A9tico_Madrid"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Atlético_Madrid">Atlético Madrid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Atlético Madrid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hasselbaink was bought by Spanish club <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> for <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>10 million in the middle of 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The "Red-and-Whites" lost the first three <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> games of the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_La_Liga" title="1999–2000 La Liga">1999–2000 season</a>, but after Hasselbaink scored his first goal for the club to secure a point at <a href="/wiki/Real_Zaragoza" title="Real Zaragoza">Real Zaragoza</a> he continued to score important goals for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> On 30 October, he scored twice in the <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Derby" title="Madrid Derby">Madrid Derby</a> as Atlético beat <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." class="mw-redirect" title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium" title="Santiago Bernabéu Stadium">Santiago Bernabéu Stadium</a> for the first time in nine years.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He also scored against <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Nou" title="Camp Nou">Camp Nou</a>, in a 2–1 league defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Manager <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Ranieri" title="Claudio Ranieri">Claudio Ranieri</a> aimed to qualify for the Champions League, but resigned in February following poor results.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Despite this Hasselbaink shared the league's Silver Boot award with <a href="/wiki/Catanha" title="Catanha">Catanha</a> (<a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_CF" title="Málaga CF">Málaga CF</a>), scoring only three goals fewer than top-scorer <a href="/wiki/Salva_Ballesta" title="Salva Ballesta">Salva Ballesta</a> (<a href="/wiki/Racing_de_Santander" title="Racing de Santander">Racing de Santander</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-page_141_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_141-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Atlético reached the <a href="/wiki/2000_Copa_del_Rey_Final" title="2000 Copa del Rey Final">final</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Copa_del_Rey" title="Copa del Rey">Copa del Rey</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Mestalla_Stadium" title="Mestalla Stadium">Mestalla Stadium</a>, but lost 2–1 to <a href="/wiki/RCD_Espanyol" title="RCD Espanyol">Espanyol</a>; Hasselbaink scored a late consolation goal. The club's league form did not improve following Ranieri's departure, and his successor <a href="/wiki/Radomir_Anti%C4%87" title="Radomir Antić">Radomir Antić</a> failed to prevent the club from being relegated into the <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a>. A relegation clause in his four-year contract allowed Hasselbaink to leave the club in the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-page_141_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_141-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chelsea">Chelsea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Chelsea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hasselbaink returned to the Premier League in May 2000, when he was signed by <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>, for a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chelsea_F.C._records_and_statistics" title="List of Chelsea F.C. records and statistics">club record</a> fee of £15 million, which matched the then-transfer record for an English club; he signed a four-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-chelsea_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chelsea-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> He scored on his "Blues" debut, helping them to win the <a href="/wiki/2000_FA_Charity_Shield" title="2000 FA Charity Shield">2000 FA Charity Shield</a> with a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Manager <a href="/wiki/Gianluca_Vialli" title="Gianluca Vialli">Gianluca Vialli</a> was dismissed in September, and Hasselbaink's former Madrid boss <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Ranieri" title="Claudio Ranieri">Claudio Ranieri</a> was appointed as his replacement.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Hasselbaink later stated he was "dismayed" at Vialli's dismissal, and that the players hated Ranieri and fitness coach Roberto Sassi's running-focused training methods.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Despite this Hasselbaink scored 23 goals in 35 league appearances in the <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Chelsea_F.C._season" title="2000–01 Chelsea F.C. season">2000–01 season</a>, including four goals in a 6–1 win against <a href="/wiki/Coventry_City_F.C." title="Coventry City F.C.">Coventry City</a> on 21 October;<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> he finished the season as the winner of the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Premier League Golden Boot</a>.
</p><p>At the start of the <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_Chelsea_F.C._season" title="2001–02 Chelsea F.C. season">2001–02 season</a> he earned the distinction of scoring the first competitive goal at <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a>'s new <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_Stadium" title="St Mary&#39;s Stadium">St Mary's Stadium</a> as Chelsea won 2–0 on 25 August.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On 13 March, he scored a hat-trick as Chelsea defeated <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> 4–0.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> He formed both a good friendship and a productive partnership with Icelandic striker <a href="/wiki/Ei%C3%B0ur_Gu%C3%B0johnsen" title="Eiður Guðjohnsen">Eiður Guðjohnsen</a>, scoring 29 goals in all competitions whilst Guðjohnsen scored 23 goals in a season which also saw Chelsea reach the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> final after overcoming <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>, <a href="/wiki/Preston_North_End_F.C." title="Preston North End F.C.">Preston North End</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Hasselbaink was a doubt for <a href="/wiki/2002_FA_Cup_Final" title="2002 FA Cup Final">the final</a> due to a hamstring injury, and was substituted on 68 minutes at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> as Chelsea lost 2–0 to <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C.%E2%80%93Chelsea_F.C._rivalry" title="Arsenal F.C.–Chelsea F.C. rivalry">rivals</a> Arsenal.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> His total of 23 league goals was one fewer than Golden Boot winner <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In summer 2002 the cause of his hamstring injury was discovered, and he underwent an operation to relieve a blockage in the <a href="/wiki/Artery" title="Artery">arteries</a> of his right leg which had been severely restricting circulation.<sup id="cite_ref-page_182_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_182-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> During his recovery he appeared as a pundit for <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a>'s coverage of the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-page_182_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_182-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Ranieri initiated a <a href="/wiki/Squad_rotation_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Squad rotation system">squad rotation system</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Chelsea_F.C._season" title="2002–03 Chelsea F.C. season">2002–03 season</a>, but focused the team around <a href="/wiki/Gianfranco_Zola" title="Gianfranco Zola">Gianfranco Zola</a>, which limited Hasselbaink's playing time.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a> agreed an £8 million transfer for Hasselbaink in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_English_football_transfers_winter_2002%E2%80%9303" title="List of English football transfers winter 2002–03">January transfer window</a> after months of negotiations but was dismissed before the transfer went through and the deal subsequently collapsed.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Though the attack was focused on Zola throughout the season Hasselbaink managed to score 15 goals in 44 games, only one goal less than Zola.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Chelsea_F.C._season" title="2003–04 Chelsea F.C. season">2003–04 season</a> he scored 18 goals in all competitions which, despite the arrival of new strikers <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Mutu" title="Adrian Mutu">Adrian Mutu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Crespo" title="Hernán Crespo">Hernán Crespo</a>, made him <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chelsea_F.C._seasons" title="List of Chelsea F.C. seasons">top-scorer at the club</a> for the third time in four years. On 27 March, his 32nd birthday, Hasselbaink came on as a 60th-minute substitute for <a href="/wiki/Geremi" title="Geremi">Geremi</a> and scored a hat-trick as Chelsea came from behind to beat <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a> 5–2 at <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Bridge_(stadium)" title="Stamford Bridge (stadium)">Stamford Bridge</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Chelsea finished the season in second place and reached the semi-finals of the Champions League; Hasselbaink played in both <a href="/wiki/Two-legged_tie" title="Two-legged tie">legs</a> of the semi-final defeat to <a href="/wiki/AS_Monaco_FC" title="AS Monaco FC">AS Monaco</a>, as Chelsea lost 5–3 on aggregate.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middlesbrough">Middlesbrough</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Middlesbrough">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 2004, Hasselbaink turned down approaches from <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rangers_F.C." title="Rangers F.C.">Rangers</a> and instead joined <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough_F.C." title="Middlesbrough F.C.">Middlesbrough</a> on a two-year contract after a free transfer.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Due to several other internationals being signed by the club at the time, he predicted that Middlesbrough could qualify for the Champions League.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> On 14 August, he scored on his debut for the club in a 2–2 draw with <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Riverside_Stadium" title="Riverside Stadium">Riverside Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Middlesbrough_F.C._season" title="2004–05 Middlesbrough F.C. season">2004–05 season</a> he finished as the club's top-scorer with 13 goals in 36 Premier League games, including a hat-trick in a 4–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ewood_Park" title="Ewood Park">Ewood Park</a> on 16 October.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> A seventh-place league finish was enough for the club to qualify for the following year's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a>.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Middlesbrough_F.C._season" title="2005–06 Middlesbrough F.C. season">2005–06 season</a> he scored ten goals in 22 league games and scored eight goals in 22 cup appearances. He helped <a href="/wiki/Steve_McClaren" title="Steve McClaren">Steve McClaren</a>'s "Boro" to defeat <a href="/wiki/Xanthi_F.C." title="Xanthi F.C.">Xanthi</a> (<a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>), <a href="/wiki/Grasshopper_Club_Z%C3%BCrich" title="Grasshopper Club Zürich">Grasshopper Club Zürich</a> (<a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>), <a href="/wiki/FC_Dnipro" title="FC Dnipro">Dnipro</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>), <a href="/wiki/PFC_Litex_Lovech" title="PFC Litex Lovech">Litex</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>), <a href="/wiki/VfB_Stuttgart" title="VfB Stuttgart">VfB Stuttgart</a> (<a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>), <a href="/wiki/A.S._Roma" title="A.S. Roma">A.S. Roma</a> (<a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>), <a href="/wiki/FC_Basel" title="FC Basel">FC Basel</a> (Switzerland) and <a href="/wiki/FC_Steaua_Bucure%C8%99ti" class="mw-redirect" title="FC Steaua București">Steaua București</a> (<a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>) en route to the <a href="/wiki/2006_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="2006 UEFA Cup Final">UEFA Cup final</a>. In the final Middlesbrough were beaten 4–0 by Spanish club <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Philips_Stadion" title="Philips Stadion">Philips Stadion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The cup final proved to be Hasselbaink's last appearance for the club, as new manager <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Southgate" title="Gareth Southgate">Gareth Southgate</a> decided to release him in July 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charlton_Athletic">Charlton Athletic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Charlton Athletic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After a potential move to <a href="/wiki/Celtic_F.C." title="Celtic F.C.">Celtic</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Premier_League" title="Scottish Premier League">Scottish Premier League</a> broke down,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Hasselbaink joined his fourth Premier League team, <a href="/wiki/Charlton_Athletic_F.C." title="Charlton Athletic F.C.">Charlton Athletic</a>, on a free transfer in July 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Soon after joining the club, he was charged by <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">the FA</a> with improper conduct and/or bringing the game into disrepute for his claiming Chelsea paid players a bonus after the 2004 <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> win over Arsenal; a Premier League inquiry into what would have been illegal bonus payments found no evidence to support the claims, which were denied by Chelsea.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal for the "Addicks" against his old team Chelsea in a 2–1 defeat at Stamford Bridge on 9 September.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> After seven games without a goal, Hasselbaink scored against yet another of his former clubs, Middlesbrough on 13 January, a game which Middlesbrough went on to win 3–1.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> He was released by Charlton at the end of the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Charlton_Athletic_F.C._season" title="2006–07 Charlton Athletic F.C. season">2006–07 season</a> having scored only four goals in 29 games, with half of his goal tally coming against <a href="/wiki/EFL_League_One" title="EFL League One">League One</a> side <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield_F.C." title="Chesterfield F.C.">Chesterfield</a> in the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cardiff_City">Cardiff City</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Cardiff City">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hasselbaink was on the verge of joining <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a> side <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> in August 2007, but the club later withdrew their offer.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Instead <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/Peter_Ridsdale" title="Peter Ridsdale">Peter Ridsdale</a>, who worked with Hasselbaink at Leeds United, brought him to Cardiff on a one-year deal, putting him in a veteran strike partnership with <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Fowler" title="Robbie Fowler">Robbie Fowler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Manager <a href="/wiki/Dave_Jones_(footballer,_born_1956)" title="Dave Jones (footballer, born 1956)">Dave Jones</a> said that Hasselbaink initially took time to settle and become match fit but despite being a demanding player his professionalism was ultimately a positive influence.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> On 19 September, Hasselbaink scored his first goal for Cardiff with a 20-yard low drive in the 2–1 league defeat to <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ninian_Park" title="Ninian Park">Ninian Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> He was nominated for the Player of the Round in the Fifth Round of the FA Cup after scoring an impressive goal against <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> He remained as a regular starter for the "Bluebirds" throughout the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Cardiff_City_F.C._season" title="2007–08 Cardiff City F.C. season">2007–08 season</a>, and made appearances in five of the six matches Cardiff played to reach the <a href="/wiki/2008_FA_Cup_Final" title="2008 FA Cup Final">FA Cup final</a>. In the final Cardiff lost 1–0 to <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a>; Hasselbaink played 70 minutes before being substituted for <a href="/wiki/Steven_Thompson_(Scottish_footballer)" title="Steven Thompson (Scottish footballer)">Steve Thompson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> As the season finished he entered talks to extend his stay at Cardiff, however he left the club in July 2008 following a dispute over pay.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hasselbaink came to the attention of <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a> manager <a href="/wiki/Guus_Hiddink" title="Guus Hiddink">Guus Hiddink</a> whilst playing in England for Leeds United, and made his international debut on 27 May 1998 in a 0–0 draw in a friendly with <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a> at the <a href="/wiki/GelreDome" title="GelreDome">GelreDome</a> in <a href="/wiki/Arnhem" title="Arnhem">Arnhem</a>; he came on as a 61st-minute substitute for <a href="/wiki/Marc_Overmars" title="Marc Overmars">Marc Overmars</a>. On 1 June he scored his first goal in a 5–1 friendly victory over <a href="/wiki/Paraguay_national_football_team" title="Paraguay national football team">Paraguay</a>, and a few days later scored his second goal in another 5–1 friendly victory over <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-page_104_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_104-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> He was part of the Dutch squad for the <a href="/wiki/1998_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1998 FIFA World Cup">1998 FIFA World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, as back-up to established international strikers <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Kluivert" title="Patrick Kluivert">Patrick Kluivert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Bergkamp" title="Dennis Bergkamp">Dennis Bergkamp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pierre_van_Hooijdonk" title="Pierre van Hooijdonk">Pierre van Hooijdonk</a> and wingers <a href="/wiki/Boudewijn_Zenden" title="Boudewijn Zenden">Boudewijn Zenden</a> and Marc Overmars.<sup id="cite_ref-page_104_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_104-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> With other strikers not fully fit, Hasselbaink started the opening game against <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Stade_de_France" title="Stade de France">Stade de France</a>, but missed a scoring opportunity in the 0–0 draw and was taken off for Bergkamp after 65 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Kluivert was sent off in the match but Bergkamp was played as the only striker in the next game against <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_football_team" title="South Korea national football team">South Korea</a>, and van Hooijdonk was taken off the bench to replace him.<sup id="cite_ref-page_106_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_106-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In the third group game against <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Stade_Geoffroy-Guichard" title="Stade Geoffroy-Guichard">Stade Geoffroy-Guichard</a> Hasselbaink came on for Bergkamp after 78 minutes, which was to be his last appearance at the tournament as Kluivert returned from suspension to leave Hasselbaink as Hiddink's fourth choice forward; Netherlands ended the tournament in fourth place.<sup id="cite_ref-page_106_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-page_106-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hiddink resigned and was replaced by his assistant <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rijkaard" title="Frank Rijkaard">Frank Rijkaard</a>, who rarely picked Hasselbaink at international level. He next played on 18 August 1999, alongside Kluivert and <a href="/wiki/Ruud_van_Nistelrooy" title="Ruud van Nistelrooy">Ruud van Nistelrooy</a> in a friendly against <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a>; he was taken off for <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Seedorf" title="Clarence Seedorf">Clarence Seedorf</a> and the game ended 0–0.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> He next appeared six months later, playing ten minutes against <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> and 70 minutes against <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a>, and despite van Nistelrooy being injured Hasselbaink was not selected for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2000" title="UEFA Euro 2000">UEFA Euro 2000</a> as the five forwards chosen were Bergkamp, Kluivert, van Hooijdonk, <a href="/wiki/Roy_Makaay" title="Roy Makaay">Roy Makaay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_van_Vossen" title="Peter van Vossen">Peter van Vossen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> He had been part of the 25 man initial squad but, along with <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Ooijer" title="André Ooijer">André Ooijer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Winston_Bogarde" title="Winston Bogarde">Winston Bogarde</a>, was not chosen for the final 22.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Louis_van_Gaal" title="Louis van Gaal">Louis van Gaal</a> rated Hasselbaink more highly than Rijkaard, meaning more chances at international level when van Gaal took over as manager in July 2000. Hasselbaink scored against <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a> in a 2–1 win at the <a href="/wiki/Estadio_de_La_Cartuja" title="Estadio de La Cartuja">Estadio de La Cartuja</a> on 15 November 2000 but both he and Spanish captain <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Hierro" title="Fernando Hierro">Fernando Hierro</a> were sent off for fighting late in the game.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> On 24 March 2001, he scored in a 5–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Andorra_national_football_team" title="Andorra national football team">Andorra</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Mini_Estadi" title="Mini Estadi">Mini Estadi</a>, and four days later converted a penalty in a draw with <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Est%C3%A1dio_das_Antas" title="Estádio das Antas">Estádio das Antas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> On 25 April he scored in his third successive <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_2" title="2002 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group 2">World Cup qualifying</a> game, in a 4–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_national_football_team" title="Cyprus national football team">Cyprus</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Philips_Stadion" title="Philips Stadion">Philips Stadion</a>. He later played against <a href="/wiki/Estonia_national_football_team" title="Estonia national football team">Estonia</a> (twice), <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a>; he scored a penalty past Denmark in a 1–1 draw at <a href="/wiki/Parken_Stadium" title="Parken Stadium">Parken Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Netherlands did not qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2002_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2002 FIFA World Cup">2002 FIFA World Cup</a> as they finished four points behind Portugal and Ireland.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dick_Advocaat" title="Dick Advocaat">Dick Advocaat</a> replaced van Gaal as national team manager in January 2002, and Hasselbaink remained in contention. On 21 August, he came on as a substitute in a 1–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Norway_national_football_team" title="Norway national football team">Norway</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Ullevaal_Stadion" title="Ullevaal Stadion">Ullevaal Stadion</a>, and on 7 September he scored in a 3–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Belarus_national_football_team" title="Belarus national football team">Belarus</a>, the opening <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004_qualifying_Group_3" title="UEFA Euro 2004 qualifying Group 3">qualifying</a> game for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">UEFA Euro 2004</a>; this was his last appearance for Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hasselbaink was a quick sprinter and had a powerful shot, able to shoot with his left-foot despite being primarily right-footed.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Tom Sheen, sports reporter for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> and Chelsea supporter, wrote that "[Hasselbaink] possessed one of the best strikes ever seen at Stamford Bridge, was an expert free-kick taker, great with both feet and decent in the air".<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coaching_career">Coaching career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Coaching career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In October 2009, Hasselbaink trained with <a href="/wiki/National_League_South" title="National League South">Conference South</a> side <a href="/wiki/Woking_F.C." title="Woking F.C.">Woking</a> to help keep himself fit and do some coaching.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> He then worked with <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C._Reserves_and_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="Chelsea F.C. Reserves and Academy">Chelsea's under-16 squad</a> and coached at the <a href="/wiki/Nike_Academy" title="Nike Academy">Nike Academy</a> while taking his UEFA 'B' and 'A' licences.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> From July 2011 to January 2013 he was a member of the coaching staff at <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C.">Nottingham Forest</a>, leaving the club when manager <a href="/wiki/Sean_O%27Driscoll" title="Sean O&#39;Driscoll">Sean O'Driscoll</a> was dismissed.<sup id="cite_ref-shuffle_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shuffle-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Antwerp">Royal Antwerp</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Royal Antwerp">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2013, Hasselbaink was announced as the new manager of newly relegated <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Second_Division" title="Belgian Second Division">Belgian Second Division</a> club <a href="/wiki/Royal_Antwerp_F.C." title="Royal Antwerp F.C.">Royal Antwerp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink_named_manager_of_Royal_Antwerp_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink_named_manager_of_Royal_Antwerp-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> He stated that the club was "a two or three year project" and he aimed to win promotion by playing attacking football with younger players on a reduced budget.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> He made a number of signings for the club, including former <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-19_football_team" title="England national under-19 football team">England under-19</a> international <a href="/wiki/John_Bostock" title="John Bostock">John Bostock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> He led the club to a seventh-place finish in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Belgian_Second_Division" title="2013–14 Belgian Second Division">2013–14 season</a>, before turning down a new deal at the club in May 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Burton_Albion">Burton Albion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Burton Albion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 13 November 2014, Hasselbaink was appointed manager at <a href="/wiki/EFL_League_Two" title="EFL League Two">League Two</a> side <a href="/wiki/Burton_Albion_F.C." title="Burton Albion F.C.">Burton Albion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> He signed a two-and-half-year contract, and stated that he was attracted to Burton by the club's stability.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Four days after his appointment he took charge of his first game at Burton, a 3–1 win at <a href="/wiki/Wycombe_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wycombe Wanderers F.C.">Wycombe Wanderers</a> which moved the club into fourth in the table.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> He was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/EFL_League_Two_Manager_of_the_Month" title="EFL League Two Manager of the Month">League Two Manager of the Month</a> award in January for going unbeaten in the month and leading the club to victories over promotion rivals <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury_Town_F.C." title="Shrewsbury Town F.C.">Shrewsbury Town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bury_F.C." title="Bury F.C.">Bury</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> however <a href="/wiki/Chris_Wilder" title="Chris Wilder">Chris Wilder</a> of <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Town_F.C." title="Northampton Town F.C.">Northampton Town</a> won the award.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> On 18 April, Burton won 2–1 away at <a href="/wiki/Morecambe_F.C." title="Morecambe F.C.">Morecambe</a> to earn promotion to <a href="/wiki/EFL_League_One" title="EFL League One">League One</a> for the first time in their history.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Two weeks later, Burton came from 2–1 down, with ten men following the dismissal of goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Jon_McLaughlin_(footballer)" title="Jon McLaughlin (footballer)">Jon McLaughlin</a>, to defeat <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_United_F.C." title="Cambridge United F.C.">Cambridge United</a> 3–2 at the <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Stadium" title="Abbey Stadium">Abbey Stadium</a> and win the League Two title.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> At the time of his departure Burton were top of League One.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Queens_Park_Rangers">Queens Park Rangers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Queens Park Rangers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 4 December 2015, Hasselbaink was appointed as manager of <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a> club <a href="/wiki/Queens_Park_Rangers_F.C." title="Queens Park Rangers F.C.">Queens Park Rangers</a>; he signed on a rolling contract, alongside his assistant <a href="/wiki/David_Oldfield_(footballer)" title="David Oldfield (footballer)">David Oldfield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Eight days later, he took charge of them for the first time, in a goalless draw against <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a> at <a href="/wiki/Loftus_Road" title="Loftus Road">Loftus Road</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> After the game, he commented that his team were low on confidence, and needed to be given room to express themselves and "play with freedom".<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Despite the sale of leading scorer <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Austin" title="Charlie Austin">Charlie Austin</a> earlier the same day, Hasselbaink earned his first win in charge of the "Hoops" on 16 January 2016, a 3–0 victory at <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> He guided them to a 12th-place finish, and spoke of his expectations of a busy summer in the transfer market.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> He was dismissed on 5 November 2016, with QPR in 17th place.<sup id="cite_ref-Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink_sacked_as_Queens_Park_Rangers_manager_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink_sacked_as_Queens_Park_Rangers_manager-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Northampton_Town">Northampton Town</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Northampton Town">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 4 September 2017, Hasselbaink was appointed manager of League One club <a href="/wiki/Northampton_Town_F.C." title="Northampton Town F.C.">Northampton Town</a> on a three-year deal, replacing <a href="/wiki/Justin_Edinburgh" title="Justin Edinburgh">Justin Edinburgh</a> who had been sacked after four losses from the start of the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Northampton_Town_F.C._season" title="2017–18 Northampton Town F.C. season">season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> His first game was against <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Rovers_F.C." title="Doncaster Rovers F.C.">Doncaster Rovers</a> five days later, a home tie which ended in a 1–0 victory for Northampton Town.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> He was sacked on 2 April 2018 after a loss to <a href="/wiki/Peterborough_United_F.C." title="Peterborough United F.C.">Peterborough United</a> made it nine games without a win and had the "Cobblers" in the relegation zone with five games remaining of the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Northampton_Town_F.C._season" title="2017–18 Northampton Town F.C. season">2017–18</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hasselbaink has four daughters.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> He is the younger brother of <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Hasselbaink" title="Carlos Hasselbaink">Carlos Hasselbaink</a>, and uncle of <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Hasselbaink" title="Nigel Hasselbaink">Nigel Hasselbaink</a>, both professional footballers.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Race_issues_in_management">Race issues in management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Race issues in management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hasselbaink is one of the few black football managers in England. After being hired by QPR, he was asked by <a href="/wiki/Talksport" title="Talksport">Talksport</a> if he felt that he had added responsibilities as a black manager, to which he answered:
</p>
<table class="cquote pullquote" role="presentation" style="margin:auto; border-collapse: collapse; border: none; background-color: transparent; width: auto;">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: top; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: left; padding: 10px 10px;">“
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; border: none; padding: 4px 10px;">No responsibility whatsoever. I'm a big believer that I got this job because I did well at my previous club and that I am the right man for it – that's why the club has given me the opportunity. I am black, that's not going to change. I am proud to be black and that's also not going to change. That’s how it is.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td style="width: 20px; vertical-align: bottom; border: none; color: #B2B7F2; font-size: 40px; font-family: &#39;Times New Roman&#39;, Times, serif; font-weight: bold; line-height: .6em; text-align: right; padding: 10px 10px;">”
</td></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>Shortly afterwards, <a href="/wiki/Port_Vale_F.C." title="Port Vale F.C.">Port Vale</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/Norman_Smurthwaite" title="Norman Smurthwaite">Norman Smurthwaite</a> revealed that he had rejected Hasselbaink for the vacant managerial position at his club in 2014, out of fear that <a href="/wiki/Racism_in_association_football" title="Racism in association football">racist elements of their support</a> would abuse him.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_corruption_allegations">2016 corruption allegations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 2016 corruption allegations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2016_English_football_scandal" title="2016 English football scandal">2016 English football scandal</a></div>
<p>On 28 September 2016, Hasselbaink was named and shown in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a>'</i>s sting operation involving the exposing of football management personalities engaging in improper conduct. Hasselbaink negotiated a deal to work with a fictitious Far Eastern firm looking to become involved in the transfer of footballers. Additionally, Hasselbaink, despite the conflict of interest, was open to the idea of signing players represented by the firm.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Queens Park Rangers launched an internal investigation and went on to release a statement fully backing Hasselbaink and stated that <i>The Daily Telegraph</i> failed to provide sufficient evidence regarding their sting operation.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club">Club</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Club">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
